وقبل أن ننتقل من الكلام على هذه الخطوة، نقرّر لك أنَّ غرض أهل السُّنَّة في هذا الموضع مِن تشبيه كلامه تعالى بكلامنا النَّفسي هو مجرَّد الرَّدَّ على المعتزلة القائلين بأنَّ الكلام منحصر في ذي الحروف والأصوات، وليس مرادهم تشبیه کلامه جل وعزّ بكلامنا النَّفسي في الكنه والحقيقة، وكيف يُتوهم أن كلامه تعالى مماثل لكلامنا النَّفسي مع أن كلامنا النَّفسي أيضا أعراض حادثة يوجد فيها التَّقدُّم والتأخرُ ، وطرو بعضه بعد عدم بعضه، ويوجد شيئا فشيئًا ؟ فمن توهم ذلك في كلامه تعالى فليس بينه وبين الحشوية ونحوهم من المبتدعة القائلين بأنَّ كلامه تعالى حروف وأصوات فرق ! وإنما مقصد العلماء بذكر الكلام النَّفسيّ في الشَّاهد ، النَّقض على المعتزلة في حصرهم الكلام في ذي الحروف والأصوات، فيقال لهم : يَنتَقِصُ هذا الحصر بكلامنا النَّفسي ؛ فإنَّه كلام حقيقة وليس بحرفٍ ولا صوتٍ ، وإذا صح ذلك فكلام مولانا كلام مع أنه ليس بحرف ولا صوت، فلم يقع الاشتراك بين كلام الباري وكلامنا النَّفسي إِلَّا في هذه الصفة السلبية، وهي: أنَّ كُلًّا منهما ليس بحرف ولا صوت ، أما الحقيقة فمباينة للحقيقة كلَّ المُباينة ، فَاعْرِف هذا وكُن منه على ثَبَتٍ .
And before we move on from discussion of this step, we affirm to you that the purpose of the Ahl al-Sunnah in this place in likening His speech to our inner speech (kalam nafsi) is merely to refute the Mu'tazila who say that speech is confined to that which has letters and sounds. They do not intend to liken His speech, may He be glorified and exalted, to our inner speech in essence and reality. How could it be imagined that His speech is similar to our inner speech, when our inner speech is also accidental attributes (a'rad) that occur, in which precedence and subsequence exist, and some come after the absence of others, and they come into existence little by little? So whoever imagines that regarding His speech, there is no difference between him and the Hashwiyya and their like among the innovators who say that His speech is letters and sounds. Rather, the intention of the scholars in mentioning inner speech in the witnessed world is to break the Mu'tazila's confinement of speech to letters and sounds. So it is said to them: This confinement is invalidated by our inner speech, for it is truly speech without being a letter or sound. And if that is correct, then the speech of our Lord is speech while it is not a letter or sound. So the commonality between the speech of the Creator and our inner speech is only in this negative attribute: that each of them is not a letter or sound. As for the reality, it is completely different from the reality. So know this and be firm upon it.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage clarifies the Sunni methodology in the debate on the attribute of speech. The author states that when Sunni scholars liken Allah's speech to human inner speech (kalam nafsi), they are only using this as a polemical tool to refute the Mu'tazila, who restrict speech to sounds and letters. The author emphasizes that there is no real similarity in essence or reality. Human inner speech is an accident (arad) that occurs in time, has sequence, and is created. To imagine such temporality in Allah's speech would be to fall into the error of the Hashwiyya (anthropomorphists). The sole purpose of invoking kalam nafsi is to show that speech can exist without sound or letter, thereby breaking the Mu'tazila's exclusive definition. The author concludes with a strong warning: the only commonality is the negative attribute of not being sound or letter; the realities are utterly distinct. The reader is urged to understand this point firmly.

Misconception: Some think that the Sunni doctrine of kalam nafsi means Allah's speech is like human inner speech in essence and reality.
Correction: The author clarifies that the comparison is only about the negative attribute—neither is letters or sounds—while the realities are completely different.

Checkpoint
What is the sole purpose of the Sunnis using 'kalam nafsi' in this context?
A) To prove that Allah's speech is similar to human speech.
B) To refute the Mu'tazila by showing that speech can exist without sound or letter.
C) To establish that Allah's speech is a created accident.
D) To support the Hashwiyya view.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni doctrine of kalam nafsi is a polemical tool to refute the Mu'tazila by showing that speech can exist without letters and sounds, but it does not imply any positive likeness between Allah's speech and created speech.

Refuting the Mu'tazila's View on Kalam Being Created in a Body
Author refutes Mu'tazila claim that Allah creates speech in a body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila position on divine speech as a created attribute in a body and the logical refutation against it.

Core Idea
Divine speech cannot be attributed to Allah if it inheres in a tree.

This lesson dives into a major theological disagreement: the Mu'tazila, unable to ascribe originated speech directly to Allah, claimed that Allah creates speech in a separate object. The author finds this absurd and provides a sharp logical critique, exposing the flawed reasoning behind their view.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila position carefully
Understand why they felt forced to deny that speech subsists in Allah's essence and instead claimed He creates speech in a body.
They confine speech to letters and sounds, which are originated.
2
Identify the two causes behind their view
The author lists two reasons: restricting speech to letters/sounds, and deeming it improbable that Moses could understand non-customary speech.
These causes reveal their anthropomorphic assumptions.
3
Examine the author's analogy
The author compares describing Allah as speaking while speech is in a tree to describing Muhammad as knowledgeable when knowledge is in another person.
This exposes the logical contradiction in predication.
4
Reflect on the root cause
The author concludes that the flaw is their method of measuring the unseen by the witnessed (qiyas al-gha'ib 'ala al-shahid).
This is a key critique of Mu'tazila methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخطوة الثانية: رأى المعتزلة أنَّ الله تعالى وصف نفسه بالكلام، وأنَّه كلَّمَ موسى ، فلم يجدوا مَفرًا مِن أن يثبتوا الله تعالى صفة الكلام ، لكنّهم لحصرهم الكلام في ذي الحرف والصوت رَأَوْا أَنَّ هذه الصفة غير قائمة بذاته تعالى؛ لأنَّها حادثة البتة، ولا يجوز أن تكون ذات الله تعالى مَحَلَّا للحوادث ، فقالوا: إنَّ الكلام صفة يخلقها الله تعالى في شيء من الحوادث ، فمعنى: (كلم الله تكليما) عندهم : خلق في جبل، أو شجرة، أو غيرهما، قدرة على الكلام، فكلَّم هذا الجبل أو هذه الشجرة أو غيرهما موسى ، وأسند سبحانه الكلام إلى نفسه لأنه هو خالق هذه القدرة في المتكلم، وهذا كلام لا يُقضى العجب منه، وسببه الحامل عليه أمران ، أحدهما قصرهم الكلام على ذي الحروف والأصوات ، وثانيهما: استبعادهم أن يفهم موسى كلاما غير ما تعارف . وليت شعري ! كيف يصح أن يوصف واحدٌ بوصف والمعنى الذي يدلّ عليه هذا الوصف قائم بغير الموصوف ؟ وهل هذا إلا نظيرُ أنْ نصف محمداً بالعلم مثلا فنقول: (محمد عالم) أَنَّه في حين أمي جاهل لأنَّ جاره أو أخاه أو غيرهما عالمٌ ، وإذا صح ذلك فهل يبقى للكلام معنى يُحْمَل عليه ؟ ثم ما ينكرون من أن يمنح الله تعالى موسى قدرة خاصة على فهم كلامه سبحانه ؟ ألعجز توهموه في الله تعالى وهو مانح القوى والقُدَر ؟ أم لأن الجبل أو الشجرة في نظرهم أقربُ إلى أنْ يُجْعَلا موضعاً للإعجاز من موسى ، لا ، بل هو لا ، بل هو لقصور في تصوراتهم سببه قياسهم الغائب على الشاهد !
The second step: The Mu'tazila held that Allah described Himself with speech, and that He spoke to Moses. So they found no escape from affirming for Allah the attribute of speech, but due to their confining speech to letters and sounds, they saw that this attribute does not subsist in His essence, because it is absolutely originated (hadith), and it is not permissible for the essence of Allah to be a locus for originated things. So they said: Speech is an attribute that Allah creates in some originated thing. So the meaning of 'Allah spoke to Moses' according to them is: He created in a mountain, or a tree, or other than them, a power for speech, so that mountain or tree or other spoke to Moses. And He, exalted, attributed speech to Himself because He is the Creator of that power in the speaker. And this is speech at which wonder cannot be contained. The cause leading to it is two things: one is their confining speech to letters and sounds, and the second is their considering it improbable that Moses should understand speech other than what is customary. Would that I knew! How is it valid to describe someone with a description while the meaning indicated by that description subsists in other than the described? Is this not analogous to our describing Muhammad with knowledge, for example, saying 'Muhammad is knowledgeable' while in fact he is illiterate and ignorant because his neighbor or his brother or someone else is knowledgeable? And if that is correct, does speech retain any meaning to be predicated? Then why do they deny that Allah might grant Moses a special ability to understand His speech? Is it because they imagine inability in Allah while He is the Bestower of powers and abilities? Or because in their view a mountain or tree is more deserving to be made a place for a miracle than Moses? No, it is not; rather it is due to a deficiency in their concepts, caused by their measuring the unseen by the witnessed.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the Mu'tazila's doctrine regarding the attribute of speech. The author outlines the Mu'tazila position: because they confine speech to letters and sounds, and because such speech is originated (hadith), they cannot attribute it directly to Allah's essence (lest He become a locus of accidents). Instead, they claim that Allah creates speech in some other object—like a mountain or tree—which then speaks to Moses. The speech is then attributed to Allah only as the creator of that speech. The author finds this absurd, pointing out the logical inconsistency: one cannot truthfully predicate a quality of a subject if that quality actually inheres in another. He gives the analogy of calling Muhammad 'knowledgeable' when the knowledge is actually in someone else. The author then mocks the Mu'tazila's alternative, asking why they deny that Allah could give Moses a special understanding of His direct speech. Is it because they imagine Allah's inability? Or because they think a mountain is more worthy of a miracle than a prophet? The author concludes that the root cause is their flawed methodology of measuring the unseen (al-gha'ib) by the witnessed (al-shahid).

Misconception: It is plausible for Allah's attribute of speech to be created in a tree or mountain and still be attributed to Allah.
Correction: This leads to logical absurdity because you cannot truthfully predicate a quality of a subject if that quality inheres in another; the author exposes this with the analogy of calling Muhammad knowledgeable when knowledge is in someone else.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazila as described, what does it mean when Allah is said to have spoken to Moses?
A) Allah directly spoke with His eternal speech.
B) Allah created a power of speech in a mountain or tree which then spoke to Moses.
C) Moses heard the speech of an angel.
D) Allah's speech is identical to the Qur'an recited.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila view on divine speech is logically flawed because it separates the attribute from the one described, based on a false analogy between the created and the Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your life do you confine God to what your senses and reason can perceive, like the Mu'tazila confined His speech to letters and sounds? Will you repent today and ask Allah to expand your heart beyond your limited imagination?
?
The author says it is absurd to call Muhammad 'knowledgeable' when knowledge is in another. Are you attributing to yourself qualities that belong only to Allah—like control over outcomes or self-sufficiency? How can you let go of that false attribution today?
?
If you truly believed that the Qur’an is Allah’s uncreated speech, not bound by human language as the Mu'tazila claimed, how would your relationship with it change? Will you commit to reciting a verse today with the conviction that you are hearing your Lord directly?

The Qur'an as Kalam Allah: The Mu'tazila Dilemma on Createdness
Author presents the Mu'tazila dilemma on the Qur'an's createdness using consensus and textual evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila's dilemma that equates the recited Qur'an with kalam Allah, thereby arguing for its createdness, and the textual evidence they use.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila trap: if recited words are God's speech, they must be created.

In this passage, the author presents the third step of the argument: the consensus of the ummah that the Qur'an is kalam Allah. However, the Mu'tazila seize upon the fact that the Qur'an we recite and write is made of originated words and letters. They pose a dilemma: either these recited words are kalam Allah (hence created) or they are not (contradicting explicit Quranic and Companion texts). The author lays out their challenge without yet giving the refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the consensus statement
Start by reading the opening lines where the author states the unanimous agreement of the ummah from the time of the Prophet that the Qur'an is the speech of Allah.
This sets the foundation for the discussion.
2
Understand the Mu'tazila's dilemma
Identify the two horns of the dilemma: (1) if the Arabic words we recite are kalam Allah, then kalam Allah is originated (hadith); (2) if they are not kalam Allah, then the texts calling them kalam Allah are contradicted.
The Mu'tazila assume identity between the eternal attribute and its temporal expression.
3
Analyze the textual evidence
Examine the Quranic verse (9:6) and the saying of Aisha that the Mu'tazila use to support their claim that the recited words are indeed called kalam Allah.
These texts are the basis for the second horn of the dilemma.
4
Reflect on the missing solution
Notice that the passage ends with the dilemma. Think about what the Ash'ari response might be: distinguishing between the eternal attribute of speech and its temporal, created expressions.
This prepares you for the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخطوة الثالثة: اتفقت كلمة هذه الأمة من لدن رسول الله على أنّ القرآن كلام الله تعالى ، وورد ذلك في القرآن نفسه وفي الحديث وفي كلام الصحابة رضوان الله تعالى عليهم، والقرآن اسم لهذه الألفاظ العربية التي نتلوها بألسنتنا ، ونكتبها بأيدينا، وهذه الألفاظ وهذه الكتابة حادثة ؛ فقال المعتزلة : إذا كانت هذه الألفاظ وهذه الكتابة كلام الله كان كلام الله تعالى حادثا وهو ما ندعيه ، وإذا قلتم : ليست هذه الألفاظ وهذه الكتابة كلام الله ؛ كنتم قد خالفتم نصوص القرآن ونصوص الأحاديث، فإنا وجدنا الله تعالى يسمي ما نقرؤه بألسنتنا ويسمعه بعضنا من بعض: كلام الله ، انظر إلى قوله سبحانه: ﴿وَإِنْ أَحَدٌ مِّنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ اسْتَجَارَكَ فَأَجِرْهُ حَتَّى يَسْمَعَ كَلَمَ اللهِ ﴾ [التوبة : ٦] ، ووجدنا الصحابة يسمون ما نكتبه بأيدينا كلام الله ، انظر إلى قول عائشة رضي الله تعالى عنها ما بين دفتي المصحف كلام الله تعالى .
The third step: The word of this ummah from the time of the Messenger of Allah has agreed that the Qur'an is the speech of Allah. That has been reported in the Qur'an itself, in the hadith, and in the sayings of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. The Qur'an is a name for these Arabic words which we recite with our tongues and write with our hands. And these words and this writing are originated (hadith). So the Mu'tazila said: If these words and this writing are the speech of Allah, then the speech of Allah is originated, which is what we claim. And if you say that these words and this writing are not the speech of Allah, then you have contradicted the texts of the Qur'an and the texts of the hadith. For we have found that Allah calls what we recite with our tongues and what we hear from one another 'the speech of Allah'. Look at His saying: 'And if any of the polytheists seeks your protection, then grant him protection so that he may hear the word of Allah' (Qur'an 9:6). And we found the Companions calling what we write with our hands 'the speech of Allah'. Look at the saying of Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her: 'What is between the two covers of the mushaf is the speech of Allah.'
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage presents the third step, dealing with the Qur'an as the speech of Allah and the Mu'tazila's argument for its createdness. The author begins by stating the consensus of the ummah that the Qur'an is kalam Allah, supported by the Qur'an, hadith, and Companions. However, the Qur'an in our experience consists of Arabic words that we recite and write—and these are undeniably originated (hadith). The Mu'tazila then pose a dilemma: if these recited words are kalam Allah, then kalam Allah is originated; if you deny they are kalam Allah, you contradict explicit texts like Surah al-Tawba 9:6 and the saying of Aisha. The author does not provide the solution here (the next part of the text is cut off), but the passage sets up the problem. The core issue is whether the eternal attribute of speech is identical to its temporal expressions. The passage ends by quoting the evidence the Mu'tazila use to force the dilemma.

The Mu'tazilite View on Divine Speech and Its Refutation
Sanusi defines the attribute of Speech and refutes the Mu'tazilite denial of its subsistence in Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite position that divine speech is created in a creature and the commentator's refutation based on logical absurdity and the error of analogizing the unseen with the witnessed.

Core Idea
Attributing speech to Allah because He creates it in a tree is like calling Muhammad knowledgeable because his neighbor knows.

This passage tackles one of the most contentious issues in Islamic theology: the nature of God's speech. The commentator first defines the attribute of Speech and then presents the Mu'tazilite view that denies it subsists in Allah. Through a powerful reductio ad absurdum, he exposes the logical flaw in their reasoning, showing that their position leads to absurd consequences.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazilite position
Read the passage to grasp why the Mu'tazilites deny speech subsists in Allah and what they propose instead. They argue speech is contingent and cannot inhere in Allah's essence, so He creates it in a creature like a mountain or tree.
2
Analyze the reductio ad absurdum
Notice how the commentator draws an analogy: if speech is attributed to Allah because it is created in another, then one could say Muhammad is knowledgeable just because his neighbor is knowledgeable. This shows the absurdity of transferring attributes.
The analogy exposes that the Mu'tazilite view would make attribute attribution arbitrary.
3
Reflect on the root cause
Identify the two reasons given for their error: restricting speech to letters and sounds, and deeming it unlikely that Moses could understand non-conventional speech. The commentator concludes their error stems from analogizing the unseen with the witnessed.
This root cause is a key methodological critique in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ه ـ صفة الكلام، تعريفها، وجهة ثبوتها الله تعالى
€
موسی
والصوت رَأَوْا أَنَّ هذه الصفة غير قائمة بذاته تعالى؛ لأنَّها حادثة البتة، ولا يجوز أن تكون ذات الله تعالى مَحَلَّا للحوادث ، فقالوا: إنَّ الكلام صفة يخلقها الله تعالى في شيء من الحوادث ، فمعنى: (كلم الله تكليما عندهم : خلق في جبل، أو شجرة، أو غيرهما، قدرة على الكلام، فكلَّم هذا الجبل أو هذه الشجرة أو غيرهما موسى ، وأسند سبحانه الكلام إلى نفسه لأنه هو خالق هذه القدرة في المتكلم، وهذا كلام لا يُقضى العجب منه، وسببه الحامل عليه أمران ، أحدهما قصرهم الكلام على ذي الحروف والأصوات ، وثانيهما: استبعادهم أن يفهم موسى كلاما غير ما تعارف . وليت شعري ! كيف يصح أن يوصف واحدٌ بوصف والمعنى الذي يدلّ عليه هذا الوصف قائم بغير الموصوف ؟ وهل هذا إلا نظيرُ أنْ نصف محمداً بالعلم مثلا فنقول: (محمد عالم) أَنَّه في حين أمي جاهل لأنَّ جاره أو أخاه أو غيرهما عالمٌ ، وإذا صح ذلك فهل يبقى للكلام معنى يُحْمَل عليه ؟
ثم ما ينكرون من أن يمنح الله تعالى موسى قدرة خاصة على فهم كلامه سبحانه ؟ ألعجز توهموه في الله تعالى وهو مانح القوى والقُدَر ؟ أم لأن الجبل أو الشجرة في نظرهم أقربُ إلى أنْ يُجْعَلا موضعاً للإعجاز من موسى ، لا ، بل هو لا ، بل هو لقصور في تصوراتهم سببه قياسهم الغائب على الشاهد !
Fifth: The attribute of Speech, its definition, and the basis of its affirmation for Allah the Most High. Moses. And the sound, they saw that this attribute does not subsist in His essence, because it is absolutely contingent, and it is not permissible that the essence of Allah the Most High be a locus for contingent events. So they said: Indeed, speech is an attribute that Allah creates in some contingent thing. So the meaning of 'Allah spoke to Moses with speech' according to them is: He created in a mountain, or a tree, or something else, a power to speak. So this mountain or this tree or something else spoke to Moses. And He, exalted, attributed the speech to Himself because He is the creator of this power in the speaker. This is a statement at which wonder cannot be exhausted. Its cause and motive are two matters: one of them is their restriction of speech to that which has letters and sounds, and the second is their deeming unlikely that Moses should understand speech other than what is customary. Would that I knew! How can one be described with a description while the meaning indicated by this description subsists in other than the described? Is this not analogous to our describing Muhammad with knowledge, for example, saying 'Muhammad is knowledgeable' while he is in fact an illiterate ignorant because his neighbor or his brother or someone else is knowledgeable? If that is valid, then does speech retain any meaning that can be carried? Then what do they deny of Allah the Most High granting Moses a special ability to understand His speech, exalted is He? Is it impotence they imagine in Allah the Most High while He is the bestower of powers and abilities? Or because the mountain or the tree is in their view more worthy to be made a place for a miracle than Moses? No, rather it is due to a deficiency in their conceptions, the cause of which is their analogy of the unseen with the witnessed!
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of Speech and refutes the Mu'tazilite position. The commentator begins by stating the topic: the attribute of Speech, its definition, and the basis for affirming it for Allah. Then he presents the Mu'tazilite view: they deny that speech subsists in Allah's essence because they consider speech to be contingent (hadith) and Allah's essence cannot be a locus for contingent events. Instead, they claim that speech is an attribute that Allah creates in some contingent entity (like a mountain or tree) and then attributes it to Himself metaphorically. For example, when Allah spoke to Moses, they say He created in a mountain a power to speak, and the mountain spoke to Moses. The commentator finds this astonishing. He identifies two reasons for their error: 1) they restrict speech to that which consists of letters and sounds, and 2) they find it unlikely that Moses could understand speech that is not customary. The commentator then uses a reductio ad absurdum: if speech is attributed to someone because it is created in another, then one could say Muhammad is knowledgeable just because his neighbor is knowledgeable, which is absurd. He further questions why they deny that Allah could grant Moses a special ability to understand His speech directly, asking if they imagine impotence in Allah or prefer the mountain to be the locus of a miracle. He concludes that their error stems from their deficiency in conception by analogizing the unseen with the witnessed.

Key Terms
صفة الكلام
المعتزلة
الكلام
حادثة
محل للحوادث
الحروف والأصوات
قياس الغائب على الشاهد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Mu'tazilite view preserves God's transcendence by denying His essence is a locus for accidents.
Correction: The commentator shows their position leads to logical absurdity (attributes transferable between subjects) and is rooted in an invalid analogy between the unseen and witnessed.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazilites as described in this passage, why do they deny that speech subsists in Allah's essence?
A) Because speech is eternal and cannot be attributed to Allah
B) Because speech is contingent and Allah's essence cannot be a locus for contingent events
C) Because speech is a name for Allah's knowledge
D) Because they believe speech is not a real attribute

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite view that Allah's speech is created in a creature leads to logical absurdity, as attributes would be transferable between subjects, and it stems from an invalid analogy between the unseen and the witnessed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself restricting what Allah can do based on what you consider 'customary' or 'logical'? Where in your life are you most tempted to say, 'Allah wouldn't do that' because it doesn't fit your expectations? What would it take for you to surrender that limitation to His absolute power?
?
Sanusi shows that an error in theology can stem from thinking too analogically about Allah. In your own worship or understanding of Allah, where might you be projecting human limits onto Him? Pause and identify one belief you hold about Allah that could be a subtle form of qiyas al-gha'ib 'ala al-shahid. Will you actively seek correction from revelation today?
?
The author mocks the Mu'tazilite view as absurd, but their intention was to protect Allah's transcendence. When you encounter a theological position that seems obviously wrong, do you consider the good intention behind it? What is the state of your heart when you disagree with a fellow Muslim's belief? Are you more eager to correct or to understand them first?

The Consensus on the Quran as Allah's Speech and the Mu'tazilite Challenge
Consensus on Quran as Allah's speech and Mu'tazilite objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the universal consensus that the Quran is Allah's speech and how the Mu'tazilites used this to argue for its contingency.

Core Idea
The Quran is Allah's speech, but the Mu'tazilites twisted this truth to deny its eternity.

This passage begins by establishing a foundational point: the entire Muslim community from the Prophet's time has agreed that the Quran is the speech of Allah. The commentator then introduces the Mu'tazilite argument that if the Quran we recite is Allah's speech, it must be contingent like all other physical things. This sets the stage for the Sunni response, which we will see in the next lesson.

Guided Path
1
Read the consensus claim
Read the opening statement that the ummah has agreed that the Quran is Allah's speech. Note the sources: Quran, hadith, and Companions.
2
Understand the Mu'tazilite argument
The Mu'tazilites argue that if the written and recited words are Allah's speech, then that speech must be contingent (hadith). They present a dilemma: either it is Allah's speech (and thus contingent) or it is not (contradicting texts).
3
See the evidence they cite
They cite Quranic verse (9:6) and the saying of Aisha to prove that the recited/written words are called 'speech of Allah'.
4
Note the Sunni premise
The Ahl al-Sunna respond based on their first principle, which will be explained next. This lesson ends with their introduction.
The first principle is the distinction between mental and verbal speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخطوة الثالثة: اتفقت كلمة هذه الأمة من لدن رسول الله الله على أنّ القرآن كلام الله تعالى ، وورد ذلك في القرآن نفسه وفي الحديث وفي كلام الصحابة رضوان الله تعالى عليهم، والقرآن اسم لهذه الألفاظ العربية التي نتلوها بألسنتنا ، ونكتبها بأيدينا، وهذه الألفاظ وهذه الكتابة حادثة ؛ فقال المعتزلة : إذا كانت هذه الألفاظ وهذه الكتابة كلام الله كان كلام الله تعالى حادثا وهو ما ندعيه ، وإذا قلتم : ليست هذه الألفاظ وهذه الكتابة كلام الله ؛ كنتم قد خالفتم نصوص القرآن ونصوص الأحاديث، فإنا وجدنا الله تعالى يسمي ما نقرؤه بألسنتنا ويسمعه بعضنا من بعض: كلام الله ، انظر إلى قوله سبحانه: ﴿وَإِنْ أَحَدٌ مِّنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ اسْتَجَارَكَ فَأَجِرْهُ حَتَّى يَسْمَعَ كَلَمَ اللهِ ﴾ [التوبة : ٦] ، ووجدنا الصحابة يسمون ما نكتبه بأيدينا كلام الله ، انظر إلى قول عائشة رضي الله تعالى عنها ما بين دفتي المصحف كلام الله تعالى .
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة بناءً على أصلهم الأوَّلِ كلامُ الله تعالى يطلق على: الكلام النفسي القديم الذي هو صفة قديمة قائمة بذاته تعالى، ويطلق أيضا على الكلام اللفظي لا بمعنى أنه قائم به، بل بمعنى أنه خلقه على نظمه، وليس لأحد في أصل تركيبه كسب، وإطلاقه على هذين المعنيين من قبيل المشترك اللفظي ، أو من قبيل المشترك المعنوي، أو من قبيل الحقيقة والمجاز ؛ فهو حقيقة في النفسي مجاز في اللفظي من باب إطلاق اللفظ على الدال. والقرآن الكريم الذي نتلوه بألسنتنا ونكتبه ويسمعه بعضنا من بعض هو: كلام الله تعالى اللفظي، على المعنى الذي ذكرناه ، وهو المعنى الذي يسمعه المستجير بالرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وكل من أنكر أن ما بين دفتي المصحف كلام الله فهو كافر، نعم ، لو قال قائل: إن ما بين دفتي المصحف ليس كلام الله ، وهو يريد أن ما بين دفتي المصحف ليس هو الصفة القائمة بذاته تعالى لم يكفر بذلك، وقد نهى العلماء أن يقال: «القرآن حادثُ» اعترافهم بكون مع الألفاظ المتلوة والكتابة حادثة ، والسِّرُّ في هذا النهي أنَّ لفظ القرآن يطلق مجازا على الصفة القائمة بذات الله تعالى، فخافوا أن يتوهم متوهم أنَّ المقصود بقول القائل: (القرآن حادث) أنَّ الصفة القائمة بذاته حادثة ، فلدفع هذا التوهم نَهوا عن أن تطلق هذه العبارة إلا في مقام التعليم مع بيان ما يراد بها ، وهذا يفسر لنا إصرار شيخ السنة الإمام أحمد بن حنبل على أن يقول: القرآن (قديم ورضاه بالضرب والتعذيب ، والسَّجن ، في سبيل هذا الإصرار وامتناعه أنْ يقولَ: «القرآن حادث ؛ لأنه خافَ أن يفهم العامةُ هذا المعنى الذي تُوهِمُه هذه العبارة ؛ ويكون هو قدوتهم في هذا وحجتهم عند الله تعالى ، رحمه الله تعالى ورضي عنه ، وأثابه عن وتورعه أحسنَ ما يُجزي به المُخلصين.
Third step: The word of this ummah has agreed, from the time of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, that the Qur'an is the speech of Allah the Most High. And that has been reported in the Qur'an itself, in the hadith, and in the speech of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. The Qur'an is a name for these Arabic words that we recite with our tongues and write with our hands. And these words and this writing are contingent. So the Mu'tazilites said: If these words and this writing are the speech of Allah, then the speech of Allah the Most High is contingent, which is what we claim. And if you say: These words and this writing are not the speech of Allah, then you have contradicted the texts of the Qur'an and the texts of the hadiths. For we find that Allah the Most High calls what we recite with our tongues and what some of us hear from others 'the speech of Allah'. Look at His saying, exalted is He: 'And if any of the polytheists seeks your protection, then grant him protection so that he may hear the word of Allah' (Qur'an 9:6). And we find the Companions calling what we write with our hands 'the speech of Allah'. Look at the saying of 'A'isha, may Allah be pleased with her: 'What is between the two covers of the mushaf is the speech of Allah the Most High.' And the Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a said, based on their first principle, that the speech of Allah the Most High is applied to: the eternal mental speech (al-kalam al-nafsi al-qadim) which is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, and it is also applied to verbal speech (al-kalam al-lafzi), not in the sense that it subsists in Him, but in the sense that He created it according to its order, and no one has any acquisition in its original composition. Its application to these two meanings is either from the category of homonymy (al-mushtarak al-lafzi), or from the category of synonymy (al-mushtarak al-ma'nawi), or from the category of literal and metaphorical ('ayn al-haqiqa wa al-majaz). So it is literal in the mental and metaphorical in the verbal, from the category of applying the word to the indicator. The Noble Qur'an that we recite with our tongues, write, and hear from one another is: the verbal speech of Allah the Most High, according to the meaning we mentioned. And that is the meaning that the one seeking refuge with the Messenger, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, hears. And whoever denies that what is between the two covers of the mushaf is the speech of Allah is a disbeliever. Yes, if someone says: 'What is between the two covers of the mushaf is not the speech of Allah,' and he means that what is between the two covers of the mushaf is not the attribute subsisting in His essence, he does not become a disbeliever by that. And the scholars forbade saying 'the Qur'an is contingent' (al-Qur'an hadith), acknowledging that the recited words and writing are contingent. The secret in this prohibition is that the word 'Qur'an' is applied metaphorically to the attribute subsisting in the essence of Allah the Most High. So they feared that someone might mistakenly think that the speaker's intention by saying 'the Qur'an is contingent' is that the attribute subsisting in His essence is contingent. To ward off this misunderstanding, they forbade uttering this expression except in a teaching context with clarification of what is meant by it. And this explains to us the insistence of the imam of the Sunna, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, on saying that the Qur'an is eternal (qadim), and his acceptance of beating, torture, and imprisonment for the sake of this insistence, and his refusal to say 'the Qur'an is contingent', because he feared that the general public would understand this meaning that this expression suggests, and he would be their example in this and their argument before Allah the Most High. May Allah have mercy on him, be pleased with him, and reward him for his piety the best reward with which He rewards the sincere.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a presentation of the Sunni position on the Quran as the speech of Allah, distinguishing between the eternal mental speech (kalam nafsi) and the created verbal speech (kalam lafzi). The commentator begins by stating the consensus (ijma') of the ummah that the Quran is Allah's speech, citing evidence from the Quran, hadith, and the Companions. The Mu'tazilites then argue that if the Quran (the words and writing we have) is Allah's speech, then it must be contingent because those words are contingent, and if we deny it is His speech, we contradict the texts. The Sunni response is that the term 'speech of Allah' is applied in two ways: 1) to the eternal mental attribute called 'kalam nafsi', which subsists in Allah's essence, and 2) to the created verbal expression called 'kalam lafzi', which is not an attribute in Allah but is created by Him according to its order. This application can be homonymous, synonymous, or literal-metaphorical. The commentator then explains that the Quran we recite and hear is the verbal speech, and denying that it is Allah's speech (in this sense) is disbelief. However, if someone denies it is the eternal attribute, they are not a disbeliever. The scholars forbade saying 'the Quran is contingent' because the word 'Quran' is sometimes used metaphorically for the eternal attribute, and saying it is contingent could be misunderstood as applying to that attribute. This explains Imam Ahmad's insistence on saying the Quran is eternal (qadim) and his refusal to say it is contingent, even under persecution, to prevent this misunderstanding.

القرآن
حادث
المعتزلة
الصحابة

What does the commentator state as the consensus of the ummah?
A) That the Quran is created

C) That the Quran is the speech of Allah
D) That the Quran is unrecited

Key Takeaway
The entire Muslim community agrees that the Quran is Allah's speech, but the Mu'tazilites used this fact to argue for its createdness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you genuinely feel that you are hearing the speech of your Creator, or has daily familiarity made it feel like ordinary words? What would change in your heart if you truly internalized that every Arabic syllable is a direct communication from Allah to you?
?
The Mu'tazilites used rational arguments to deny the eternity of Allah's speech. Reflect: Are there any points in your faith where your own reasoning has led you to question or reinterpret clear texts? What steps can you take to ensure that revelation always holds primacy over your intellect?
?
The entire ummah from the time of the Prophet agreed that the Qur'an is Allah's speech. Yet today, many Muslims follow scholars who break from this consensus. Do you feel a pull towards novel or minority opinions that contradict the mainstream? How does that affect your attachment to the community of believers and your trust in the collective guidance of the ummah?

The Kalam Nafsi and Kalam Lafzi Distinction
Definition of kalam nafsi and lafzi and their linguistic relationship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni distinction between eternal mental speech (kalam nafsi) and created verbal speech (kalam lafzi), and how the term 'speech of Allah' applies to both.

Core Idea
Allah's speech is twofold: an eternal attribute in His essence and its temporal verbal expression.

Having introduced the Mu'tazilite challenge, the commentator now presents the Sunni response. The key is a distinction between two meanings of 'speech of Allah': the eternal mental attribute (kalam nafsi) and the created verbal expression (kalam lafzi). The commentator explains how the term is applied to these two meanings, considering different linguistic categories like homonymy and metaphor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two meanings
The passage defines two meanings of 'speech of Allah': 1) the eternal mental attribute subsisting in His essence, and 2) the created verbal speech not subsisting in Him but created by Him.
2
Understand the first meaning (kalam nafsi)
The eternal mental speech is an attribute of Allah that is qadim (eternal) and subsists in His essence. It is not created.
3
Understand the second meaning (kalam lafzi)
The verbal speech is the created words that we recite and hear. It is not an attribute of Allah but something He created.
No one has any acquisition (kash) in its original composition.
4
Explore the linguistic application
The passage then discusses how the term is applied to these two meanings: it can be homonymy (mushtarak lafzi), synonymy (mushtarak ma'nawi), or literal/metaphorical. It concludes that it is literal for the mental and metaphorical for the verbal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخطوة الثالثة: اتفقت كلمة هذه الأمة من لدن رسول الله الله على أنّ القرآن كلام الله تعالى ، وورد ذلك في القرآن نفسه وفي الحديث وفي كلام الصحابة رضوان الله تعالى عليهم، والقرآن اسم لهذه الألفاظ العربية التي نتلوها بألسنتنا ، ونكتبها بأيدينا، وهذه الألفاظ وهذه الكتابة حادثة ؛ فقال المعتزلة : إذا كانت هذه الألفاظ وهذه الكتابة كلام الله كان كلام الله تعالى حادثا وهو ما ندعيه ، وإذا قلتم : ليست هذه الألفاظ وهذه الكتابة كلام الله ؛ كنتم قد خالفتم نصوص القرآن ونصوص الأحاديث، فإنا وجدنا الله تعالى يسمي ما نقرؤه بألسنتنا ويسمعه بعضنا من بعض: كلام الله ، انظر إلى قوله سبحانه: ﴿وَإِنْ أَحَدٌ مِّنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ اسْتَجَارَكَ فَأَجِرْهُ حَتَّى يَسْمَعَ كَلَمَ اللهِ ﴾ [التوبة : ٦] ، ووجدنا الصحابة يسمون ما نكتبه بأيدينا كلام الله ، انظر إلى قول عائشة رضي الله تعالى عنها ما بين دفتي المصحف كلام الله تعالى .

Third step: The word of this ummah has agreed, from the time of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, that the Qur'an is the speech of Allah the Most High. And that has been reported in the Qur'an itself, in the hadith, and in the speech of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. The Qur'an is a name for these Arabic words that we recite with our tongues and write with our hands. And these words and this writing are contingent. So the Mu'tazilites said: If these words and this writing are the speech of Allah, then the speech of Allah the Most High is contingent, which is what we claim. And if you say: These words and this writing are not the speech of Allah, then you have contradicted the texts of the Qur'an and the texts of the hadiths. For we find that Allah the Most High calls what we recite with our tongues and what some of us hear from others 'the speech of Allah'. Look at His saying, exalted is He: 'And if any of the polytheists seeks your protection, then grant him protection so that he may hear the word of Allah' (Qur'an 9:6). And we find the Companions calling what we write with our hands 'the speech of Allah'. Look at the saying of 'A'isha, may Allah be pleased with her: 'What is between the two covers of the mushaf is the speech of Allah the Most High.' And the Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a said, based on their first principle, that the speech of Allah the Most High is applied to: the eternal mental speech (al-kalam al-nafsi al-qadim) which is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, and it is also applied to verbal speech (al-kalam al-lafzi), not in the sense that it subsists in Him, but in the sense that He created it according to its order, and no one has any acquisition in its original composition. Its application to these two meanings is either from the category of homonymy (al-mushtarak al-lafzi), or from the category of synonymy (al-mushtarak al-ma'nawi), or from the category of literal and metaphorical ('ayn al-haqiqa wa al-majaz). So it is literal in the mental and metaphorical in the verbal, from the category of applying the word to the indicator. The Noble Qur'an that we recite with our tongues, write, and hear from one another is: the verbal speech of Allah the Most High, according to the meaning we mentioned. And that is the meaning that the one seeking refuge with the Messenger, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, hears. And whoever denies that what is between the two covers of the mushaf is the speech of Allah is a disbeliever. Yes, if someone says: 'What is between the two covers of the mushaf is not the speech of Allah,' and he means that what is between the two covers of the mushaf is not the attribute subsisting in His essence, he does not become a disbeliever by that. And the scholars forbade saying 'the Qur'an is contingent' (al-Qur'an hadith), acknowledging that the recited words and writing are contingent. The secret in this prohibition is that the word 'Qur'an' is applied metaphorically to the attribute subsisting in the essence of Allah the Most High. So they feared that someone might mistakenly think that the speaker's intention by saying 'the Qur'an is contingent' is that the attribute subsisting in His essence is contingent. To ward off this misunderstanding, they forbade uttering this expression except in a teaching context with clarification of what is meant by it. And this explains to us the insistence of the imam of the Sunna, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, on saying that the Qur'an is eternal (qadim), and his acceptance of beating, torture, and imprisonment for the sake of this insistence, and his refusal to say 'the Qur'an is contingent', because he feared that the general public would understand this meaning that this expression suggests, and he would be their example in this and their argument before Allah the Most High. May Allah have mercy on him, be pleased with him, and reward him for his piety the best reward with which He rewards the sincere.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a presentation of the Sunni position on the Quran as the speech of Allah, distinguishing between the eternal mental speech (kalam nafsi) and the created verbal speech (kalam lafzi). The commentator begins by stating the consensus (ijma') of the ummah that the Quran is Allah's speech, citing evidence from the Quran, hadith, and the Companions. The Mu'tazilites then argue that if the Quran (the words and writing we have) is Allah's speech, then it must be contingent because those words are contingent, and if we deny it is His speech, we contradict the texts. The Sunni response is that the term 'speech of Allah' is applied in two ways: 1) to the eternal mental attribute called 'kalam nafsi', which subsists in Allah's essence, and 2) to the created verbal expression called 'kalam lafzi', which is not an attribute in Allah but is created by Him according to its order. This application can be homonymous, synonymous, or literal-metaphorical. The commentator then explains that the Quran we recite and hear is the verbal speech, and denying that it is Allah's speech (in this sense) is disbelief. However, if someone denies it is the eternal attribute, they are not a disbeliever. The scholars forbade saying 'the Quran is contingent' because the word 'Quran' is sometimes used metaphorically for the eternal attribute, and saying it is contingent could be misunderstood as applying to that attribute. This explains Imam Ahmad's insistence on saying the Quran is eternal (qadim) and his refusal to say it is contingent, even under persecution, to prevent this misunderstanding.

الحقيقة والمجاز

Key Takeaway
Allah's speech is twofold: an eternal attribute (kalam nafsi) and a created verbal expression (kalam lafzi), with the term applied literally to the former and metaphorically to the latter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage teaches that no human has any acquisition in the original composition of the Quran. Have you ever felt pride in your ability to recite or memorize the Quran? How should this doctrine humble you and redirect your gratitude?

The Ruling on Denying the Quran and the Prohibition of 'Contingent' Language
Rulings on denying the Quran and prohibition of 'contingent' language

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ruling on denying the Quran as Allah's speech, the nuanced prohibition of saying 'the Quran is contingent', and the reason behind Imam Ahmad's stance.

Core Idea
Denying the recited Quran is disbelief, but calling it 'contingent' is prohibited to avoid misunderstanding about the eternal attribute.

After establishing the kalam nafsi/lafzi distinction, the commentator addresses practical rulings. He clarifies that affirming the recited Quran as Allah's speech is necessary, but denying it is disbelief. However, he also explains the scholars' prohibition of saying 'the Quran is contingent' (al-Qur'an hadith) because the word 'Quran' can metaphorically refer to the eternal attribute. This leads into the historical stance of Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal.

Guided Path
1
Understand the ruling on denial
Whoever denies that the mushaf contains Allah's speech is a disbeliever. But a careful exception: if someone means it is not the eternal attribute, they are not a disbeliever.
2
Learn the prohibition of 'contingent'
The scholars forbade saying 'the Quran is contingent' (hadith) even though the recited words are contingent, because the word 'Quran' can be metaphorically used for the eternal attribute.
3
See the fear behind the prohibition
They feared that saying it might be misunderstood as referring to the eternal attribute, so they forbade it except in teaching contexts with clarification.
4
Appreciate Imam Ahmad's stance
Imam Ahmad insisted on saying 'the Quran is eternal' (qadim) and refused to say it is contingent, even under torture, to prevent public misunderstanding.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخطوة الثالثة: اتفقت كلمة هذه الأمة من لدن رسول الله الله على أنّ القرآن كلام الله تعالى ، وورد ذلك في القرآن نفسه وفي الحديث وفي كلام الصحابة رضوان الله تعالى عليهم، والقرآن اسم لهذه الألفاظ العربية التي نتلوها بألسنتنا ، ونكتبها بأيدينا، وهذه الألفاظ وهذه الكتابة حادثة ؛ فقال المعتزلة : إذا كانت هذه الألفاظ وهذه الكتابة كلام الله كان كلام الله تعالى حادثا وهو ما ندعيه ، وإذا قلتم : ليست هذه الألفاظ وهذه الكتابة كلام الله ؛ كنتم قد خالفتم نصوص القرآن ونصوص الأحاديث، فإنا وجدنا الله تعالى يسمي ما نقرؤه بألسنتنا ويسمعه بعضنا من بعض: كلام الله ، انظر إلى قوله سبحانه: ﴿وَإِنْ أَحَدٌ مِّنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ اسْتَجَارَكَ فَأَجِرْهُ حَتَّى يَسْمَعَ كَلَمَ اللهِ ﴾ [التوبة : ٦] ، ووجدنا الصحابة يسمون ما نكتبه بأيدينا كلام الله ، انظر إلى قول عائشة رضي الله تعالى عنها ما بين دفتي المصحف كلام الله تعالى .
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة بناءً على أصلهم الأوَّلِ كلامُ الله تعالى يطلق على: الكلام النفسي القديم الذي هو صفة قديمة قائمة بذاته تعالى، ويطلق أيضا على الكلام اللفظي لا بمعنى أنه قائم به، بل بمعنى أنه خلقه على نظمه، وليس لأحد في أصل تركيبه كسب، وإطلاقه على هذين المعنيين من قبيل المشترك اللفظي ، أو من قبيل المشترك المعنوي، أو من قبيل الحقيقة والمجاز ؛ فهو حقيقة في النفسي مجاز في اللفظي من باب إطلاق اللفظ على الدال. والقرآن الكريم الذي نتلوه بألسنتنا ونكتبه ويسمعه بعضنا من بعض هو: كلام الله تعالى اللفظي، على المعنى الذي ذكرناه ، وهو المعنى الذي يسمعه المستجير بالرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وكل من أنكر أن ما بين دفتي المصحف كلام الله فهو كافر، نعم ، لو قال قائل: إن ما بين دفتي المصحف ليس كلام الله ، وهو يريد أن ما بين دفتي المصحف ليس هو الصفة القائمة بذاته تعالى لم يكفر بذلك، وقد نهى العلماء أن يقال: «القرآن حادثُ» اعترافهم بكون مع الألفاظ المتلوة والكتابة حادثة ، والسِّرُّ في هذا النهي أنَّ لفظ القرآن يطلق مجازا على الصفة القائمة بذات الله تعالى، فخافوا أن يتوهم متوهم أنَّ المقصود بقول القائل: (القرآن حادث) أنَّ الصفة القائمة بذاته حادثة ، فلدفع هذا التوهم نَهوا عن أن تطلق هذه العبارة إلا في مقام التعليم مع بيان ما يراد بها ، وهذا يفسر لنا إصرار شيخ السنة الإمام أحمد بن حنبل على أن يقول: القرآن (قديم ورضاه بالضرب والتعذيب ، والسَّجن ، في سبيل هذا الإصرار وامتناعه أنْ يقولَ: «القرآن حادث ؛ لأنه خافَ أن يفهم العامةُ هذا المعنى الذي تُوهِمُه هذه العبارة ؛ ويكون هو قدوتهم في هذا وحجتهم عند الله تعالى ، رحمه الله تعالى ورضي عنه ، وأثابه عن وتورعه أحسنَ ما يُجزي به المُخلصين.
Third step: The word of this ummah has agreed, from the time of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, that the Qur'an is the speech of Allah the Most High. And that has been reported in the Qur'an itself, in the hadith, and in the speech of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. The Qur'an is a name for these Arabic words that we recite with our tongues and write with our hands. And these words and this writing are contingent. So the Mu'tazilites said: If these words and this writing are the speech of Allah, then the speech of Allah the Most High is contingent, which is what we claim. And if you say: These words and this writing are not the speech of Allah, then you have contradicted the texts of the Qur'an and the texts of the hadiths. For we find that Allah the Most High calls what we recite with our tongues and what some of us hear from others 'the speech of Allah'. Look at His saying, exalted is He: 'And if any of the polytheists seeks your protection, then grant him protection so that he may hear the word of Allah' (Qur'an 9:6). And we find the Companions calling what we write with our hands 'the speech of Allah'. Look at the saying of 'A'isha, may Allah be pleased with her: 'What is between the two covers of the mushaf is the speech of Allah the Most High.' And the Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a said, based on their first principle, that the speech of Allah the Most High is applied to: the eternal mental speech (al-kalam al-nafsi al-qadim) which is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, and it is also applied to verbal speech (al-kalam al-lafzi), not in the sense that it subsists in Him, but in the sense that He created it according to its order, and no one has any acquisition in its original composition. Its application to these two meanings is either from the category of homonymy (al-mushtarak al-lafzi), or from the category of synonymy (al-mushtarak al-ma'nawi), or from the category of literal and metaphorical ('ayn al-haqiqa wa al-majaz). So it is literal in the mental and metaphorical in the verbal, from the category of applying the word to the indicator. The Noble Qur'an that we recite with our tongues, write, and hear from one another is: the verbal speech of Allah the Most High, according to the meaning we mentioned. And that is the meaning that the one seeking refuge with the Messenger, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, hears. And whoever denies that what is between the two covers of the mushaf is the speech of Allah is a disbeliever. Yes, if someone says: 'What is between the two covers of the mushaf is not the speech of Allah,' and he means that what is between the two covers of the mushaf is not the attribute subsisting in His essence, he does not become a disbeliever by that. And the scholars forbade saying 'the Qur'an is contingent' (al-Qur'an hadith), acknowledging that the recited words and writing are contingent. The secret in this prohibition is that the word 'Qur'an' is applied metaphorically to the attribute subsisting in the essence of Allah the Most High. So they feared that someone might mistakenly think that the speaker's intention by saying 'the Qur'an is contingent' is that the attribute subsisting in His essence is contingent. To ward off this misunderstanding, they forbade uttering this expression except in a teaching context with clarification of what is meant by it. And this explains to us the insistence of the imam of the Sunna, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, on saying that the Qur'an is eternal (qadim), and his acceptance of beating, torture, and imprisonment for the sake of this insistence, and his refusal to say 'the Qur'an is contingent', because he feared that the general public would understand this meaning that this expression suggests, and he would be their example in this and their argument before Allah the Most High. May Allah have mercy on him, be pleased with him, and reward him for his piety the best reward with which He rewards the sincere.

Commentary

The commentator begins by stating the consensus (ijma') of the ummah that the Quran is Allah's speech, citing evidence from the Quran, hadith, and the Companions. This application can be homonymous, synonymous, or literal-metaphorical. The commentator then explains that the Quran we recite and hear is the verbal speech, and denying that it is Allah's speech (in this sense) is disbelief. Why the Attribute of Speech Requires Revealed Evidence
Commentator explains the primary proof for the attribute of Speech is transmitted.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that for the attributes of Speech, Hearing, and Sight, the primary proof is revelation (transmitted evidence), not reason, and how this distinguishes them from other divine attributes.

Core Idea
For speech, hearing, and sight, revelation leads; reason follows.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies a key methodological principle in kalam: not all divine attributes are proven by the same means. While most attributes like power and knowledge are established primarily through rational proof, the attributes of Speech, Hearing, and Sight rely primarily on transmitted evidence from revelation. This distinction is crucial for understanding the unique nature of these attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the commentator's emphasis on 'know first that the relied-upon evidence is transmitted proof.'
Notice the phrase 'المعتمد في إثبات هذه الصفة الله تعالى هو الدليل السمعي'.
2
Identify the two categories of attributes
The passage divides divine attributes into two groups: (1) Speech, Hearing, and Sight, where transmitted proof is primary, and (2) other attributes, where rational proof is primary. Find these two categories in the text.
Look for 'بخلاف غير الكلام والسمع والبصر من الصفات'.
3
Reflect on the rationale
Ask yourself why these three attributes might be different. The passage does not give the reason, but invites you to consider that the author will indicate it later. This highlights a deeper theological point about the nature of these attributes.
This step connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكلام على دليل وجوب اتصاف الله تعالى بالكلام فنقول لك: اعلم أوّلا أنَّ المعتمد في إثبات هذه الصفة الله تعالى هو الدليل السمعي كما سينبه عليه المؤلف بقوله: «بذا أتانا السمع: إما وحده ، وإما هو مع الدليل العقلي، على أن يكون الدليل العقلي مؤيدا ومؤكدا للدليل النقلي ، بخلاف غير الكلام والسمع والبصر من الصفات، فإنَّ المعتمد في الاستدلال عليها هو الدليل العقلي: إما وحده وإما هو مع الدليل النقلي، على أن يكون الدليل النقلي مؤيدا ومؤكدًا للدليل العقلي ، ثم اعلم أنَّ الدليل النقلي على ثبوت صفة الكلام الله تعالى آيات من الكتاب ، وأحاديثُ رويت بالطَّرُقِ الصَّحيحة عن الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم .
And as for the discourse on the proof for the necessity of Allah the Most High being described with speech, we say to you: Know first that the relied-upon [evidence] in establishing this attribute for Allah the Most High is the transmitted proof (al-dalil al-sam'i), as the author will alert to by his saying: 'By this the transmitted evidence has come to us: either alone, or it is with the rational proof, such that the rational proof is a supporter and confirmer for the transmitted proof.' Contrary to other attributes besides speech, hearing, and sight – for the relied-upon [evidence] in reasoning for them is the rational proof: either alone or it is with the transmitted proof, such that the transmitted proof is a supporter and confirmer for the rational proof. Then know that the transmitted proof for the establishment of the attribute of speech for Allah the Most High consists of verses from the Book (the Qur'an) and hadiths transmitted through authentic chains from the Messenger, may Allah bless him and grant him peace.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage discusses the proof for the attribute of Speech. The commentator begins by directing the reader: 'Know first that the relied-upon [evidence] in establishing this attribute for Allah is the transmitted proof (al-dalil al-sam'i).' He then cites the author (the original text of Jawharat al-Tawhid) who indicated that the transmitted proof alone or supported by rational proof is primary for this attribute. For other attributes (like power, will, knowledge), the primary proof is rational, with transmitted proof as support. However, for speech, hearing, and sight, the primary proof is transmitted. The commentator then specifies that the transmitted proofs for the attribute of speech are verses from the Qur'an and authentic hadiths.

Key Takeaway

The Primacy of Revelation for the Attribute of Speech
States the primacy of transmitted evidence for the attribute of speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the attribute of Allah's speech is proven primarily through transmitted evidence (sam'i) rather than reason, and be able to cite key scriptural proofs.

Core Idea
The attribute of speech is known through revelation, not reason alone.

This passage from the commentary on Jawharat al-Tawhid explains a crucial distinction: while most divine attributes are established by rational proof, the attribute of speech—along with hearing and sight—is primarily proven by transmitted evidence (the Qur'an and Sunnah). The author provides the rationale and then cites specific verses and hadith. Let's examine the argument and its scriptural basis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the full Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Notice the author's emphasis on 'al-dalil al-sam'i' (transmitted evidence) as the primary proof for speech.
Pay attention to the contrast with other attributes that rely on rational evidence.
2
Understand the distinction between sam'i and 'aqli evidence
The passage explains that for speech, hearing, and sight, the relied-upon evidence is transmitted (sam'i), with reason playing a supporting role. For other attributes, reason is primary with transmitted evidence as support. Compare the two cases.
This distinction is a key principle in Sunni kalam.
3
Examine the scriptural proofs
Identify the two Quran verses (4:164 and 2:30) and the hadith of the Night Journey. Notice how each directly attributes speech to Allah or implies it through dialogue.
Also note the general argument that all messengers conveyed revelation, proving speech across religions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكلام على دليل وجوب اتصاف الله تعالى بالكلام فنقول لك: اعلم أوّلا أنَّ المعتمد في إثبات هذه الصفة الله تعالى هو الدليل السمعي كما سينبه عليه المؤلف بقوله: «بذا أتانا السمع: إما وحده، وإما هو مع الدليل العقلي، على أن يكون الدليل العقلي مؤيدا ومؤكدا للدليل النقلي، بخلاف غير الكلام والسمع والبصر من الصفات، فإنَّ المعتمد في الاستدلال عليها هو الدليل العقلي: إما وحده وإما هو مع الدليل النقلي، على أن يكون الدليل النقلي مؤيدا ومؤكدًا للدليل العقلي، ثم اعلم أنَّ الدليل النقلي على ثبوت صفة الكلام الله تعالى آيات من الكتاب، وأحاديثُ رويت بالطَّرُقِ الصَّحيحة عن الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم. أما الآيات فمنها قوله تعالى: ﴿وَكَلَّمَ اللَّهُ مُوسَى تَكْلِيمًا﴾ [النساء: ١٦٤]، وقوله جلت كلمته: ﴿وَإِذْ قَالَ رَبُّكَ لِلْمَلَائِكَةِ إِنِّي جَاعِلٌ فِي الْأَرْضِ خَلِيفَةً قَالُوا أَتَجْعَلُ فِيهَا مَن يُفْسِدُ فِيهَا وَيَسْفِكُ الدِّمَاءَ وَنَحْنُ نُسَبِّحُ بِحَمْدِكَ وَنُقَدِّسُ لَكَ قَالَ إِنِّي أَعْلَمُ مَا لَا تَعْلَمُونَ﴾ [البقرة: ۳۰]. وأما الأحاديث فمنها: حديث المعراج، وفيه أنَّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «خاطب ربَّه، وأنه فرض عليه خمسين صلاة، وأنه ما زال يراجع ربه حتى قال له: هُنَّ خمس وهُنَّ خمسون» وما زالت الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام يحدثون عن ربهم أنه أوحى إليهم بشرع يبلغونهُ النَّاسَ؛ إما بخطابه إياهم، وإما بخطابه سبحانه ملك الوحي وهو يبلغهم عن ربهم؛ فكان ذلك آية ثبوت هذه الصفة الله تعالى في جميع الملل السماوية على لسان جميع الرسل.
And as for the discussion on the proof of the necessity of Allah being described with speech, we say to you: Know first that the relied-upon [method] in establishing this attribute of Allah is the transmitted evidence (al-dalil al-sam'i), as the author will point out with his statement: 'With this the transmitted [evidence] came to us: either alone, or together with rational evidence, on condition that the rational evidence be a supporter and confirmer for the transmitted evidence, unlike other attributes such as speech, hearing, and sight, for the relied-upon method in inferring them is rational evidence: either alone or together with transmitted evidence, on condition that the transmitted evidence be a supporter and confirmer for the rational evidence.' Then know that the transmitted evidence for the establishment of the attribute of speech for Allah are verses from the Book and hadiths reported through authentic chains from the Messenger (peace be upon him). As for the verses, among them are His statement: 'And Allah spoke to Moses with [direct] speech' (al-Nisa 4:164), and His statement, exalted be His word: 'And [mention] when your Lord said to the angels, 'Indeed, I will make upon the earth a successor.' They said, 'Will You place upon it one who causes corruption therein and sheds blood, while we exalt You with praise and declare Your perfection?' He said, 'Indeed, I know that which you do not know'' (al-Baqarah 2:30). As for the hadiths, among them is the hadith of the Night Journey (Isra'), in which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) addressed his Lord, and He obligated upon him fifty prayers, and he kept appealing to his Lord until He said to him: 'They are five and they are fifty.' And the messengers (peace and blessings be upon them) continued to relate from their Lord that He revealed to them a law which they convey to the people, either by His addressing them directly, or by His addressing the angel of revelation and he conveys to them from their Lord. And that was a sign of the establishment of this attribute of Allah in all heavenly religions upon the tongues of all the messengers.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage discusses the proof (dalil) for the necessity of Allah being described with the attribute of speech. It begins by stating that the primary authority (al-mu'tamad) in establishing this attribute is transmitted evidence (al-dalil al-sam'i), as indicated by the author of the matn (Jawharat al-Tawhid) with his phrase 'With this the transmitted [evidence] came to us...' This transmitted evidence may stand alone (i.e., purely from revelation) or be accompanied by rational evidence (al-dalil al-'aqli) that supports and confirms it. This is contrasted with other attributes besides speech, hearing, and sight, which are primarily proven by rational evidence, with transmitted evidence playing a supporting role. Then the passage provides specific scriptural evidence. From the Qur'an, two verses are cited: (1) 'And Allah spoke to Moses with [direct] speech' (4:164), which explicitly affirms speech for Allah; and (2) the verse about the creation of Adam where Allah speaks to the angels (2:30), implying speech. From the hadith, the hadith of the Night Journey (Isra') is mentioned, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) addressed his Lord and negotiated the prayers, showing direct speech. The passage also notes that all messengers conveyed revelations from Allah, either through direct address or through the angel Jibril, which proves that the attribute of speech is established in all heavenly religions through the tongues of all messengers.

الدليل العقلي
الدليل النقلي
آيات
أحاديث
صفة الكلام

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might assume that all divine attributes are proven by reason in the same way, but the attribute of speech primarily depends on revelation.
Correction: The passage clarifies that speech, hearing, and sight are established through transmitted evidence (sam'i), while other attributes rely on rational evidence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary evidence for establishing the attribute of speech for Allah?
A) Rational evidence alone.
B) Transmitted evidence (sam'i) alone or with rational support.
C) Both equally.
D) Neither; it is known necessarily.

Key Takeaway
The attribute of speech, unlike most divine attributes, is established primarily by transmitted evidence (revelation), as confirmed by explicit Quranic verses and prophetic hadith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about Allah's speech, do you primarily rely on what the Quran and Sunnah say, or do you try to rationalize it? What does your answer reveal about your heart's submission to revelation?
?
The passage says that for the attribute of speech, transmitted evidence is primary. In your daily life, do you treat the Quran as the primary source for knowing who Allah is, or do you let your own reasoning override it? Where have you placed reason above revelation?
?
The messengers conveyed Allah's speech to people. How has the speech of Allah come to you? Are you treating the Quran as a direct communication from Him, or just as a book of guidance? What would change if you truly believed that Allah is speaking to you through it?

The Relation of Divine Speech to Commands and Prohibitions
Sanusi presents the debate on the relation of divine speech to commands and prohibitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly debate on how the attribute of divine speech relates to commands and prohibitions, and how it differs from knowledge.

Core Idea
The relation of God's speech to commands depends on whether they require existence.

This passage explores a nuanced debate in kalam about the relation (ta'luq) of God's attribute of speech to commands and prohibitions. While scholars agree on the general scope of speech, they differ on whether commands and prohibitions require existing objects, leading to different views on the kind of relation speech has to them. This lesson unpacks that disagreement and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed scope of speech's relation
Notice that scholars agree speech relates to everything knowledge relates to (necessary, possible, impossible) with a pre-eternal actual relation, except for command and prohibition.
This sets the baseline.
2
Understand the root disagreement
The disagreement hinges on whether commands and prohibitions necessitate the existence of a commanded or prohibited entity (mamur/manhi).
Two groups emerge from this root.
3
Learn the two positions and their resulting relations
One group (doesn't require existence) maintains a single actual relation. The other group (requires existence) posits two relations: potential before existence, actual after.
Thus, some scholars say one relation exists; others say three.
4
Compare speech with knowledge
Both share the same scope (everything), but they differ in mode: knowledge discloses, speech indicates.
This clarifies why the relation is not identical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكلام على تعلق الكلام فنقول: اتفق العلماء على أنَّ صفة الكلام تتعلق بكل ما يتعلق به العلم من الواجب والجائز والمستحيل، تعلقا تنجيزيا قديما بالنسبة لغير الأمر والنهي، واختلفوا في تعلّق هذه الصفة بالأمر والنهي، والخلاف في هذا مبني على خلاف آخر، حاصله: هل الأمر والنهي يقتضيان مأمورًا ومنهيَّا يتوجهان إليه أو لا يقتضيان ذلك؟ فذهب قوم إلى أنهما لا يقتضيان مأمورًا ومنهيَّا، وهذا الفريق يرى تعلقا تنجيزيا قديما كتعلقه بغيرهما، وذهب فريق آخر: إلى أنَّ الأمر والنهي يقتضيان وجود مأمورٍ ومنهي يتوجهان إليه، وهذا الفريق ذهب إلى أنَّ للكلام بالنظر إلى الأمر والنهي: تعلقا صلوحيًّا قديماً قبل وجود المأمور والمنهي، وتعلقا تنجيزيا حادثا بعد وجود المأمور والمنهي؛ ومِن هنا تعلم أن من العلماء من ذهب إلى أن للكلام تعلقاً واحداً هو: التنجيزي القديم، ومنهم من ذهب إلى أن للكلام ثلاث تعلقات: أحدها تنجيزي قديم، وثانيها صلوحي قديم، وثالثها تنجيزي حادث. وتعلم أنَّ هذا الخلاف مترتب على خلاف آخر في اشتراط وجود المأمور والمنهي وعدم وجودهما. وقد علمت أيضا أنَّ الكلام مساو للعلم في المتعلَّق؛ لأن من علم أمرًا صح أن يتكلم به. والمولى سبحانه عالمٌ في الأزل بما كان، وما يكون، وما لا يكون؛ فصح أن يكلم بهما، ومع تساوي العلم والكلام فيما يتعلقان به فهما مختلفان في التعلق؛ لأن العلم يتعلق بما يتعلق به تعلق انكشاف والكلام يتعلق به تعلق دلالةٍ، فكلامه تعالى يدل على الواجب، وعلى المستحيل، وعلى الجائز.
And as for the discussion on the relation (taluq) of speech, we say: The scholars agreed that the attribute of speech relates to everything that knowledge relates to, of the necessary, the possible, and the impossible, with a pre-eternal actual relation (taluq tanjizi qadim) with respect to other than command and prohibition. And they differed concerning the relation of this attribute to command and prohibition. The disagreement in this is based on another disagreement, the summary of which: Do command and prohibition necessitate a commanded and a prohibited [entity] to which they are directed, or do they not necessitate that? One group held that they do not necessitate a commanded and a prohibited [entity], and this group sees a pre-eternal actual relation like its relation to other than them. Another group held that command and prohibition necessitate the existence of a commanded and a prohibited [entity] to which they are directed. This group held that speech, with respect to command and prohibition, has a pre-eternal potential relation (taluq suluhi qadim) before the existence of the commanded and the prohibited, and a temporal actual relation (taluq tanjizi hadith) after the existence of the commanded and the prohibited. From this you know that among the scholars are those who held that speech has one relation: the pre-eternal actual [relation]; and among them are those who held that speech has three relations: one pre-eternal actual, a second pre-eternal potential, and a third temporal actual. And you know that this disagreement is dependent on another disagreement concerning the condition of the existence of the commanded and the prohibited and their non-existence. And you also know that speech is equal to knowledge in what it relates to, because whoever knows a thing, it is correct for him to speak about it. And the Master—glorified is He—is eternally knower of what was, what will be, and what will not be; so it is correct for Him to speak about them. And with the equality of knowledge and speech in what they relate to, they differ in the [mode of] relation; because knowledge relates to what it relates to as a relation of disclosure (inkishaf), and speech relates to it as a relation of indication (dalalah). So His speech—exalted is He—indicates the necessary, the impossible, and the possible.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage deals with the relation (taluq) of the attribute of speech to its objects. It begins by noting scholarly agreement: the attribute of speech relates to everything that knowledge relates to—the necessary (wajib), the possible (ja'iz), and the impossible (mustahil)—with a pre-eternal actual relation (tanjizi qadim), except in the case of command and prohibition (amr and nahy). Regarding command and prohibition, there is a disagreement that stems from a prior dispute: Do commands and prohibitions require the existence of a commanded entity (ma'mur) and a prohibited entity (manhi) to which they are directed? One group says no, so the relation of speech to them is the same pre-eternal actual relation as to other objects. Another group says yes, they require existence; therefore, before the commanded/prohibited exist, the relation is potential (suluhi qadim), and after they exist, it becomes actual but temporal (tanjizi hadith). Thus, some scholars hold that speech has only one relation (the pre-eternal actual for all), while others hold that it has three relations: pre-eternal actual (for non-command/prohibition), pre-eternal potential (for command/prohibition before existence), and temporal actual (for command/prohibition after existence). The passage then notes that this difference depends on whether existence of the commanded/prohibited is a condition. Finally, it compares speech and knowledge: they share the same scope (everything), but differ in mode—knowledge is a relation of disclosure (inkishaf), while speech is a relation of indication (dalalah). Allah's speech indicates the necessary, the impossible, and the possible.

تعلق
تنجيزي
صلوحي
الأمر والنهي
المأمور
المنهي
انكشاف
دلالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the relation of divine speech to all objects is uniform and straightforward.
Correction: In fact, there is a significant debate about commands and prohibitions, leading to multiple types of relation (actual, potential, temporal) depending on whether the commanded/prohibited object must exist.

Checkpoint
According to those who hold that commands and prohibitions require existence, what is the relation of speech to command before the commanded exists?
A) Pre-eternal actual (tanjizi qadim).
B) Pre-eternal potential (suluhi qadim).
C) Temporal actual (tanjizi hadith).
D) There is no relation.

Key Takeaway
The relation of divine speech is not uniform; it has distinct modes (actual, potential) depending on the object and whether existence is required.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a divine command in the Quran, do you feel it is binding on you only when you are about to act (temporal actual), or do you accept that it has been directed at you pre-eternally (pre-eternal potential)? How would your obedience change if you truly believed the command was speaking to you before you existed?
?
The passage teaches that God's speech indicates (dalalah) what is necessary, impossible, and possible. Which of these categories do you struggle to accept most in your life? Are there prohibitions (impossible for you to do?) that you still try to justify? How can you rely more on the indication of His speech rather than your own reasoning?
?
Compare your reliance on God's knowledge (that He knows everything about you) with your reliance on His speech (what He commands and forbids). Which one shapes your daily choices more? If you found that you trust His knowledge but not His speech, what would that reveal about your heart? What step can you take today to align your actions with His speech?
