Proof that Perception is an Extra Attribute Beyond Knowledge
Commentator proves perception is an extra attribute using two arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that Allah's perceptions (sight, hearing, etc.) are additional attributes beyond His knowledge, based on necessary distinction and the argument from perfection.

Core Idea
Perceptions are perfections; their absence would imply deficiency, which is impossible for Allah.

Sanusi's commentator now turns to a specific divine attribute: perception (idrak). While Allah's knowledge is all-encompassing, the senses like sight and hearing seem distinct. The commentator argues that perceptions are not merely included in knowledge but are separate attributes. This lesson unpacks the rational proof for this position, drawing on the necessary distinction between knowing and perceiving, and the principle that perfection requires all perfections.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Start by reading the Arabic passage once. Notice the structure: it begins by stating the claim, then gives two reasons.
2
Understand the first proof: necessary distinction
The commentator says there is a tafriqa daruriyya (necessary distinction) between knowledge and perception. How do you distinguish between knowing something and perceiving it? Reflect on this.
3
Understand the second proof: perfection argument
Perceptions are perfections (kamalat). Every living being capable of them that lacks them would have their opposites, which are deficiencies. Since deficiency is impossible for Allah, He must possess them.
4
Apply the principle of befittingness
The passage concludes by noting that these perceptions are affirmed in a manner befitting Allah, denying any physical connection or pleasure/pain. This safeguards divine transcendence.
5
Synthesize
Summarize how the commentator proves that perceptions are extra attributes. Why is this important for understanding Allah's attributes?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم الإلهيات • إلى إثباتها; لأنَّ الإدراكات المتعلقة بهذه الأشياء زائدة على العلم بها، للتفرقة الضرورية بينهما، وأيضا هي كمالات، وكل حي قابل لها، فإذا لم يتصف بها اتصف بأضدادها، وهي نقص لأن معها فوت كمال، والنقص في حقه تعالى محال، فوجب أن يتصف سبحانه بتلك الإدراكات زائدة على علمه تعالى على ما يليق به من نفي الاتصال بالأجسام ونفي اللذات عنه تعالى والآلام.
The division of divine matters: to its affirmation [as attributes], because the perceptions related to these things are additional to knowledge, due to the necessary distinction between them, and also because they are perfections, and every living thing is capable of them, and if it is not qualified with them, it becomes qualified with their opposites, which are deficiencies because they involve the loss of perfection, and deficiency is impossible with respect to Him, may He be exalted, so it is necessary that He, glorified be He, be qualified with those perceptions as additional to His knowledge, may He be exalted, in a manner befitting Him, including denial of connection (ittisal) with bodies and denial of pleasures (ladhdhat) and pains (alam) with respect to Him, may He be exalted.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a proof (dalil) that the perceptions (idrakat) such as sight, hearing, smell, taste, touch are additional attributes (sifat za'ida) beyond knowledge (`ilm). The author begins by stating that the perceptions related to these things (i.e., the objects of perception) are additional to knowledge. The first reason is the necessary distinction (tafriqa daruriyya) between knowledge and perception in the witnessed world (shahid); since we distinguish between knowing something and perceiving it, the same applies to the unseen (gha'ib). The second reason is that perceptions are perfections (kamalat). Every living being capable of them that lacks them would have their opposites, which are deficiencies because they entail the loss of perfection. Since deficiency is impossible for God, He must be qualified with those perceptions as extra attributes beyond His knowledge, while denying any connection to bodies (ittisal) and any associated pleasures or pains, as these are not befitting Him.

Key Terms
إدراكات (perceptions)
علم (knowledge)
كمالات (perfections)
نقص (deficiency)
اتصال (connection)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Perception is just a type of knowledge; no separate attribute is needed.
Correction: The passage argues that knowledge and perception are necessarily distinct in our experience, and perceptions are perfections, so they are separate attributes.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why must God have perceptions as additional attributes beyond knowledge?
A) Because perceptions are pleasurable.
B) Because they are perfections and their absence would imply deficiency.
C) Because God's knowledge is limited without them.
D) Because the Qur'an explicitly mentions them.

Key Takeaway
Allah's perceptions are distinct attributes from His knowledge, proven by necessary distinction and the perfection argument, while safeguarding transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that Allah's perception of you is a perfection, why do you often act as if He does not see you? Is there a specific area of your life where you need to increase your awareness of His hearing and sight? What will you change today?
?
You affirm that deficiency is impossible for Allah, yet you tolerate deficiencies in your own character. What one deficiency in yourself are you most attached to, and how can you begin to replace it with the perfection that Allah has commanded?
?
Are you content with merely knowing about Allah's attributes, or do you actively seek to perceive His signs in creation and His revelation? How can you move from theoretical knowledge to a living perception of His majesty today?

The Denial of Extra Perception and the Rational Entailment Argument
The passage lists the scholars who deny extra perception and presents the rational entailment argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that some scholars deny an extra attribute of perception for Allah because it would entail physical connection, which is impossible.

Core Idea
Perception would require connection, so it cannot be an attribute of Allah.

This lesson presents the view that perception is not an extra attribute of Allah, held by several scholars including Imam al-Juwayni's father. The key argument is that perception would entail a connection (ittisal) with its objects, which is impossible for Allah. Since the consequent is impossible, the antecedent must also be impossible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholars
Read the passage and note the scholars who denied an extra attribute of perception. They include Imam Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni, Qadi Husayn, and others.
This list shows that the view was held by notable authorities.
2
Understand the rational entailment
The passage asserts a rational entailment (talazum `aqli) between perception and connection. If perception is an extra attribute, it must involve connection with its objects.
Connection (ittisal) implies physical contact, which is impossible for Allah.
3
Apply the impossibility of the consequent
Since connection is impossible for Allah, and it is a necessary consequence of the extra attribute, the attribute itself must be impossible. This is a logical argument: the impossibility of the consequent entails the impossibility of the antecedent.
This is a standard form of argument in kalam: if A implies B, and B is impossible, then A is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسمع أو لا) أي : أو ليس له تعالى صفة زائدة تسمى الإدراك كما ذهب إليه من شيوخه: والده الإمام أبو محمد الجويني، والقاضي حسين، والقاضي أبو الطيب الطبري، الحديث من أبي بكر أحمد بن محمد بن الحارث الأصبهاني، ومنصور بن رامش، وغيرهم كثير، الخلاف في زيادة صفة الإدراك، جمع; لما أن بينها وبين الاتصال بمتعلقاتها تلازما عقليا; فلا يتصور انفكاكها عنه، والاتصال مستحيل عليه تعالى، واستحالة اللازم توجب استحالة الملزوم، ولأن إحاطة العلم بمتعلقاتها كافية عن إثباتها حيث لم يرد بها سمع ولا دل عليها فعله تعالى، ودعوى أنه تعالى لو لم يتصف بها اتصف بأضدادها فاسدة; لمنافاة العلم لتلك الأضداد، وقد وجب اتصافه تعالى به.
And [some say]: 'No, he does not have an extra attribute called perception (idrak), as held by his teachers: his father Imam Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni, Qadi Husayn, Qadi Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari, the traditionist Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Harith al-Asbahani, Mansur ibn Rash [Ramish?], and many others.' The disagreement over the extra attribute of perception: gathered? [possibly meaning 'the response is'] because there is a rational entailment (talazum `aqli) between it [i.e., the supposed attribute] and connection (ittisal) with its objects; thus its disconnection from connection cannot be conceived. And connection is impossible for Him, may He be exalted, and the impossibility of the consequent necessitates the impossibility of the antecedent. And because the encompassment of knowledge (`ilm) of its objects suffices for its affirmation, since no revealed text (sam`) has come regarding it, nor do His actions indicate it. And the claim that if He were not qualified with it He would be qualified with its opposites is invalid, because knowledge (al-`ilm) contradicts those opposites, and He is necessarily qualified with knowledge.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage presents the disagreement over whether perception (idrak) is an extra attribute beyond knowledge. First, it lists those who deny it: Imam al-Juwayni's father, Qadi Husayn, Qadi Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari, and others. Then it gives the refutation, which is the argument against the extra attribute. The refutation offers several arguments. First, there is a rational entailment between the supposed attribute of perception and connection (ittisal) with physical objects; since connection is impossible for God, the attribute leading to it must also be impossible. Second, God's knowledge is sufficient to encompass the objects of perception, so there is no need for an extra attribute, especially as no revealed text (sam`) supports it and God's actions do not indicate it. Third, the claim that the lack of perception would lead to its opposites (like blindness or deafness) is invalid because God's knowledge contradicts those opposites; His knowledge already covers all, so He cannot be described with such deficiencies. Thus, the conclusion is that God is qualified with knowledge alone, and perception is not an extra attribute.

Key Terms
إدراك (perception)
زيادة (extra)
اتصال (connection)
تلازم عقلي (rational entailment)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the rational entailment mentioned in the passage?
A) Between perception and knowledge
B) Between perception and connection
C) Between connection and revelation
D) Between knowledge and revelation

Key Takeaway
Perception as an extra attribute is denied because it would require physical connection, which is impossible for Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson uses rational entailment to deny an attribute that would imply physicality in Allah. Are there any beliefs I hold about Allah that inadvertently involve physical or human-like qualities? How can I actively purify my understanding to align with tawhid?
?
The scholars here were willing to deny a commonly-held notion based on rational proof. Am I ready to give up any comfortable but incorrect ideas about Allah if sound reasoning shows they are impossible? What example in my own thinking needs this correction today?
?
If I truly believe that Allah is free from all physical attributes, then how does this affect my worship and my relationship with Him? Does my heart fully accept that He is beyond any comparison, or do I still imagine Him in limited ways?

Sufficiency of Knowledge and Refutation of the Opposites Claim
The passage gives two additional refutation arguments: sufficiency of knowledge and invalidity of the opposites claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the arguments that knowledge is sufficient for perception and that the claim of opposites is invalid.

Core Idea
Allah's knowledge covers all, negating any need for a separate perception attribute.

In this passage, the author continues the refutation by presenting two additional arguments: first, that Allah's knowledge (ilm) is already sufficient to encompass all objects of perception, so no extra attribute is needed, especially without textual or empirical evidence. Second, the claim that lacking perception would imply opposites like blindness is invalid because knowledge contradicts such opposites.

Guided Path
1
Understand the argument that knowledge suffices
Allah's knowledge encompasses all objects of perception. Therefore, there is no need for a separate attribute of perception; knowledge already does the job.
This is a principle of economy: no need to posit extra attributes when one suffices.
2
Note the lack of evidence
No revealed text (sam') or action of Allah indicates an extra perception attribute. This absence of evidence further supports the denial.
In kalam, attributes are established either by reason or revelation. Here both are absent.
3
Refute the opposites claim
The objection that lacking perception would lead to its opposites (e.g., blindness) is invalid because Allah's knowledge contradicts those opposites. Since Allah has perfect knowledge, He cannot have deficiencies.
Knowledge is incompatible with ignorance or sensory deficiencies.

Source Text

?
